<div id="review_300090968" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300090968" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300090968?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Crystal Starr Light by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4529669-willow">Willow </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=editor-wanted">editor-wanted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=amazon-vine">amazon-vine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=ha-ha-ha-no-really">ha-ha-ha-no-really</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=i-whine-therefore-i-am">i-whine-therefore-i-am</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=romance-in-disguise">romance-in-disguise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=don-t-quit-your-day-job">don-t-quit-your-day-job</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=idiot-protagonist">idiot-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=so-bad-it-s-good">so-bad-it-s-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=what-the-hell-did-i-just-read">what-the-hell-did-i-just-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300090968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3181013695433701191">First off, I'd like to thank the magnificent Willowfaerie for her magnificent <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350431154' rel='nofollow noopener'>review</a> of this...erm...book that inspired me to get off my @$$ and finally review this Amazon Vine ARC.<br/><br/>Secondly, I was PLAUGED with this book from Amazon Vine. I couldn't find a MASQUE anywhere that could PREVENT this DISEASE.<br/><br/>Thirdly, while I have adopted a new 25% rule, I didn't use it on this book for two reasons. Number 1, I like to make an effort to read Vine books all the way through, and Number 2, I was too engro</span>
  <span id="freeText3181013695433701191" style="display:none">First off, I'd like to thank the magnificent Willowfaerie for her magnificent <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350431154" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> of this...erm...book that inspired me to get off my @$$ and finally review this Amazon Vine ARC.<br><br>Secondly, I was PLAUGED with this book from Amazon Vine. I couldn't find a MASQUE anywhere that could PREVENT this DISEASE.<br><br>Thirdly, while I have adopted a new 25% rule, I didn't use it on this book for two reasons. Number 1, I like to make an effort to read Vine books all the way through, and Number 2, I was too engrossed by the WTF in this book to give up.<br><br>With that out of the way...<br><br>OH. MY. GOD! This book was dreadful. My 100+ status updates (filled with gif spam) can kinda of show the mind-numbingly awfulness of this book. I almost don't know where to begin.<br><br>No, wait, I do. Araby Worth...LESS. Araby is our protagonist, our main character. I would call her a "heroine", but she's more like "heroin". There is very little redeemable or likeable or even just interesting about her.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><i>Woe is me, my life is so horrible - I haven't gone to Hot Topic in three whole days!</i><br><br>In the agonizing beginning half, she whines about EVERYTHING. She hates on her "best friend", April (who, BTW, is by far one of the best characters in this book). She complains about her friend saving her from jumping - and then whines when a boy she likes saves her out of obligation. She whines that her dad hates her - and then he takes her on a walk, or gives her a poetry book, or basically looks the other way as she proceeds to betray him and expose him to his enemies. She hates on her mother, whom she considers "pathetic" and "weak". She whines about the death of her brother. Oh, and she makes really odd promises - such as not to experience anything her brother won't. Which might not seem to weird until you start realizing the rules. Sex and kissing is off-limits; drug use and wearing corsets apparently is OK (Hey, maybe Finn would have wanted to wear a whalebone corset, who knows?!). Honestly, I wasn't surprised at the vow; I was more surprised at how it was so general, but then applied only to the specific instance of kissing or having sex - very convenient for sexual tension, eh?<br><br>And "sexual tension" there is. In spades. Because like ALL Young Adult books - paranormal, urban fantasy, dystopians, and all the books, such as this one, that try to pass off as any of the previous ones - HAS to have a Romantic Triangle. AT LEAST.<br><br>The two carboard cutouts - I MEAN!! - romantic interests that plague - POPULATE! - this novel are BoyToy1 (Will) and BoyToy2 (Elliott). (I refuse to acknowledge they have names and "character".) They are basically the only characters that Araby ever respects or trusts or believes - even when she claims she doesn't trust or believe them. The only real difference between the two is that BT1 has two CUTE ADORABLE WIDDLE siblings - you know, to show how kind-hearted and tender and caring he is, while also providing some much needed DRAMAZ over masques and sh!t - and the other is a pyschopath. No really - he dangles Araby over crocodile-infested waters and tells her that, while he may be falling in love with her, he would totally feed her to the crocs, because Rebellion before broads, man. I mean, wouldn't YOU TOTES fall in love with a guy like that? (Oh, right, she doesn't "love" BT2 - she just MIGHT be believing/trusting him. While she listens to his every order and never asks any questions and basically lets him push her around. Yeah, I'm not buying that either.) But he has SCARS! He was held prisoner by his uncle, Prospero! He was ABUSED! Therefore, he needs a little woman to make all his boo-boos go away and feel better!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/653837.gif" width="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More of this book is dedicated to Araby being with one of these lifeless hunks of manflesh than to any "dystopia" or "steampunk". In fact, there are several wasted pages with Araby and Will basically playing house with his CUTE WIDDLE siblings (who don't act like any children I've ever seen before). All while her mother has been captured and her father is in hiding. Because the best time to snuggle up to BT1 while wearing his shirt to sleep in is when your family is missing!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380373210ra/726687.gif" width="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh, God, the villains. God, the villains. I swear, Prospero and the Reverend came from "Dummies Guide to Villains". The only way to make them worse would be to have them twirl their mustaches and chuckle, as they kicked a sick puppy down a staircase into crocodile-infested waters. Seriously. Prospero even has villain teeth - nice and stained.<br><br>But - and I know this is hard to believe - I didn't hate all the characters. Mother, Father, and April were actually my favorites. Mother I felt was misunderstood. In actuality, I see her as a tough woman (we find out that she went through a lot of crap and didn't burden her worthLESS daughter with the details). She worries over her daughter, whom she sees is in pain, but she doesn't know how to help her. So she does her best with the tools at hand. (Not to mention, she's probably also coping with Finn's death?) Father was awesome; he's that bad @$$ absent-minded professor. He really cares about his daughter, but he blames himself for all the deaths and the death of his son, so he locks himself away physically and emotionally. When he does try to reach out to his daughter, his daughter is so locked in herself, she just shuts him down. And then there's April. I didn't think I'd add her to my favorite characters, but when she makes quips about the redness of her lipstick and then shoulders a musket and fires down a ladder on an airship and HITS the guy she was aiming at - yeah, why wasn't she the protagonist again?<br><br>I guess the story is supposed to be about rebelling against Prospero and the Reverend. But that would require the book to be a dystopian. Instead, this is yet another romance masquerading as a dystopian. Throw in a villain, make it hundreds of years in the future, have people dying and voila! Insta-dystopian!<br><br>Most of the book is watching Araby be an idiot. The first half, she stumbles around Clubs, acting like a moron and forcing other people to save her. The second half, she lets a man she barely knows tell her what to do, expose her AND HER FAMILY to danger, and forces other people to save her. Oh, and this guy she lets order her around? That would be psychopath BT2 - you know, the one who said he'd throw her to the crocs for his Rebellion. Yeah. As I was reading one stupid thing after another that she doesn't, I couldn't help but think:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349887ra/703798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now, let's talk about diseases. And masques. And how the frak does this one work? So, lemme get this straight: the people wear masques to prevent disease. OK, I get that. But then, there is no way to keep the inflicted away from the healthy? Uh...quarantine anyone? And then everyone takes off their frakkin' masque for anything - to breathe (because you can't???), to kiss, because it's itchy, because it doesn't look good with leather - I mean, seriously, if this is the big way to keep from getting sick, then WEAR THE DAMN MASQUE ALREADY! This isn't rocket science!<br><br>But no, wait! Now people are squeamish about touching infected. Because now it's transmitted via contact?<br><br><blockquote>I suspect the germs crawled off his lank brown hair and infested everything.</blockquote><br><br>RIGHT! That's how disease works! Germs ride on a person's hair and when they meet their victim, they get off and leap onto their victim, thus infecting them!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373211i/726688.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then add in how apparently BT1 and Araby can ride in an air balloon ABOVE the disease, and I have absolutely no clue about anything anymore. I honestly think the disease is transmittable via PlotContrivancitis.<br><br>I'm starting to run out of steam, but I have one more area I must address before I end this novel-length review. Steampunk. Steampunk has a very unique feel and look. In short, steampunk should look like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373211i/726689._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>or this:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>or this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373211i/726691.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NOT this:<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><i>It has clocks on it - STEAMPUNK!</i><br><br>or this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373211i/726693._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>See?! Whalebone corset! TOTALLY steampunk!</i><br><br>or this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373211i/726694._SY540_.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Anything Abe Lincoln must be Steampunk...right?</i><br><br>I don't read just to snark on books and give them bad reviews. I really want to love every book that I read. But this book just did not mesh with me. At all. The most enjoyment I got out of it was all the gaping I was doing at how dumb Araby acted and the completely predictable nature of the book. I personally don't recommend reading this unless you are up for snark bait. I most certainly will not be seeking out the next book in this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3181013695433701191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_278710588" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278710588" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278710588?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-girl">point-of-view-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278710588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16093709833822556656">I'll start this review by admitting the two reasons I read this book at all: <br/><br/>1) It draws heavily on the inspirations of Edgar Allan Poe (also known as 'The Man') and I assumed that <i>Masque</i> would be either a more detailed retelling or some sort of revision of the original<br/>2) It was highly recommended by <i>Nevermore</i> author Kelly Creagh, the current reigning champion for a Poe-inspired novel<br/><br/><i>Masque of the Red Death</i> has some obvious similarities to the original work. The first 100 or so pages reminded me</span>
  <span id="freeText16093709833822556656" style="display:none">I'll start this review by admitting the two reasons I read this book at all: <br /><br />1) It draws heavily on the inspirations of Edgar Allan Poe (also known as 'The Man') and I assumed that <i>Masque</i> would be either a more detailed retelling or some sort of revision of the original<br />2) It was highly recommended by <i>Nevermore</i> author Kelly Creagh, the current reigning champion for a Poe-inspired novel<br /><br /><i>Masque of the Red Death</i> has some obvious similarities to the original work. The first 100 or so pages reminded me very much of Poe's original tale: there's death and despair everywhere, the character feels such overwhelming grief that all she wants to do is escape, and there's that clear negligence among the upper class (epitomized here by Araby's self-absorbed friend, April, as well as the other members of the Debauchery Club). But then...the tone completely shifts and I learn about this revolution and this coup against the Prince. Even Prospero is different: rather than an apathetic fop, as I was expecting, I got a conniving psychopath. Now don't get me wrong, psychopaths are interesting (the Queen of Hearts from <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i> is a ton of crazy fun), but this guy was practically useless. No reason or motive or anything.<br /><br />I tried <b>so hard</b> to like this book. And on the surface, there's nothing really wrong with it and nothing that would keep me from liking it. I want to point out that for a story that has a "Debauchery Club," it was pretty tame. Surprisingly tame. But <i>Masque</i> ended up thoroughly confusing me on many levels. I don't even know what to call this book: it's not a dystopian, it's not really a paranormal, and frankly, one airship and a bunch of corsets doesn't qualify as a steampunk in my eyes. So what is this, exactly? A neo-Gothic horror story? There wasn't enough 'horror,' though, because halfway through the novel the focus shifts away from decay and despair to seeds of revolution. To be honest, it read like a story with no clear direction, like it couldn't make up its mind if it was going to be character-driven, or plot driven. And so (for me), it basically failed at both. By contrast, one of the powerful elements of Poe's works is his dark and melancholy mood. Dark, but with just a hint of suspense, of something big that's about to happen. That mood did not carry over into <i>Masque of the Red Death</i> the way it did in <i>Nevermore</i>. <br /><br />This next section deals specifically with the ARC version:<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am not exaggerating: on every page - EVERY PAGE - there was at least one line of dialogue that had no speaker attached to it, and usually it was more than one. It's hard to get absorbed in the story when I can't figure out who's speaking. Another thing: characters would just *poof* appear out of nowhere. Like, in one sentence, Araby would be alone in a room, and in literally the next sentence, she's having a conversation with someone else. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />But for me, the biggest "thing" about <i>Masque</i> was the characters' sheer lack of motivation and the way they related to each other. I actually get why Araby would want to waste away her days in the Debauchery Club. That's hardly a stretch of the imagination. What I don't get is why she gets involved in a plot to overthrow the Prince (that's not a spoiler) or why other characters did what they did, if that makes sense. The other big "thing" about this book was the stark contrast between character descriptions and character actions. None of the characters had any clearly-defined personalities and as a result, everybody seemed pretty schizophrenic. In one chapter, a girl would be a complete airhead and quintessential 'mean girl' - a few chapters later, the same girl would be giving orders and plotting to overthrow the Prince. And that would have been near genius (the whole 'appearance vs. reality' motif) if I got the feeling that the author did it on purpose. But I didn't get that feeling. The feeling I got is that <i>Masque of the Red Death</i> is populated by characters that lack any defining personalities or motivations. They just do and say whatever suits the current mood. The whole thing was rather bizarre.<br /><br />What else haven't I mentioned? There is a quasi-love triangle, but up until the last two chapters, I didn't mind it at all, because Araby clearly had a 'favorite' and did a good job of giving the other guy the cold shoulder. And I will say that Ms. Griffin gives readers a new experience with her triangle: instead of giving the protagonist two gorgeous, perfect (and submissive) guys, she ends up giving the protagonist a choice between <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[two jerkface assholes. One is a drug-dealing, romp-loving psycho, and the other is a liar and a betrayer <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Interesting. <br />And much like <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i>, there was a twist at the end that I didn't see coming. Also like <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i>, I did not care for the twist, and thought it was actually handled in a very sloppy manner. I genuinely believe that <i>having a major twist at the end ONLY WORKS if it makes SENSE. Otherwise, it's just useless and confusing. And this twist, like I said, was one of the sloppiest-written twists I've ever read.</i><br /><br />Overall, <i>Masque of the Red Death</i> didn't hold up for me. Like I said, I tried very hard to like this book (harder than I've tried for any other book in a long time) and I compliment Bethany Griffin on taking one of Edgar Allan Poe's best-known stories and giving it a unique spin. I know that there will be many who will love this book, and in this case, I would say judge it for yourself. For me, though, it takes a special book to hold up Poe's dynamic legacy, and this just wasn't it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16093709833822556656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review278710588">

<div id="review_233337859" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233337859" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233337859?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=arc-e-galley">arc-e-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233337859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17638457266042088340"><b>The figure was tall and gaunt, and shrouded from head to foot in the habiliments of the grave. The mask which concealed the visage was made so nearly to resemble the countenance of a stiffened corpse that the closest scrutiny must have had difficulty in detecting the cheat. And yet all this might have been endured, if not approved, by the mad revelers around. But the mummer had gone so far as to assume the type of the Red Death. His vesture was dabbled in blood--and his broad brow, with all the </b></span>
  <span id="freeText17638457266042088340" style="display:none"><b>The figure was tall and gaunt, and shrouded from head to foot in the habiliments of the grave. The mask which concealed the visage was made so nearly to resemble the countenance of a stiffened corpse that the closest scrutiny must have had difficulty in detecting the cheat. And yet all this might have been endured, if not approved, by the mad revelers around. But the mummer had gone so far as to assume the type of the Red Death. His vesture was dabbled in blood--and his broad brow, with all the features of the face, was besprinkled with the scarlet horror.</b><br />-<i>The Masque of Red Death, Edger Allan Poe</i><br /><br />Red Death has caused extensive destruction and ruin, population is eradicating and the country has long devastated. Red Death is deadly plague taking over the society, threatening to wipe out every single life from country. People have no choice but paying extremely high price for a mask that can protect them from this contamination. Araby is one of the privileged people who belongs to rich society and her parent has enough money to buy one mask for her. At one of her nights in the Debauchery Club, a place kept the sickness out where wealthy people of town can enjoy their evenings without mask and fear of plague, Araby met Will, the terribly handsome proprietor of the club and Elliott, the wickedly smart aristocrat. But neither of them are what they appears to be, both have secrets and plans of their own. As she was more drawn to these boys, she found herself struggling with her feelings and thrust into a secret world full of danger and mayhem.<br /><br /><b>The Redness and Horror of Blood</b><br /><br />As a big Poe fan, I wouldn’t dare to compare this book with original Masque of Red Death, but I must say it was a very brave attempt to remake the master piece. Author adapted the theme from Poe’s The Masque of Red Death, twisted it very artfully and mingled it with her own thoughts, thus creating an imaginative and gruesome story of death and desire. <br />Griffin’s Mask of Red Death set in post apocalyptic era where the city architecture, stream carriages, clothing style everything very much resembles to time period when the original classic took place, 19th century. <br />The Masque of Red Death follows many traditions of gothic fiction; a dark tale represents a falling society that controlled by mad Prince Prospero who was as brutal as the disease. He intended to secure his own luxury and safety, indifferent to the sufferings of the population. The whole country in misbalance; streets are disturbed with rebellion and inevitability of death. <br /><br /><b>Darkness, Decay and Desire</b><br /><br /><b>We are vulnerable with our lanterns shining brightly in darkness.</b><br />-<i>The Masque of Red Death, Brittany Griffin</i><br /><br />As a protagonist Araby was not that appealing character as I thought her to be, slightly disconnected and confused, I could not relate myself to her. She was less concern about the circumstance and consequences of dark situations around her. We saw her character developed towards the end but not much that could please me. <br />She was drawn to Will and depended on Elliot; both the boys were different from each other with own secrets to keep. Elliot was nephew of prince Prospero with mysterious personality and desperate to avenge his parent’s death, boldly resisting authority to any danger. On the other side Will was charming by his presence and caught my eyes in his first appearance. As story progressed, more secrets unfolds and I was haunted by the stabbing truth of both the boys especially the more I found out about Will, the more my jaw dropped leaving me temporarily incapable of breathing.<br /><br />I enjoyed Araby as the voice of narration. The Masque of Red Death is slow moving, detailed and literary version of the original one. Araby’s story melds beautifully with Prospero’s using it as the background. The ending bears an ambiguous message to readers, made them wanting more though I really doubt there will be any sequel.<br />Brittany Griffin was successful in creating a wickedly dark and alluring tale with horror of death and decay harmonized with hope and love. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17638457266042088340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_288585730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288585730" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288585730?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Absolutely everyone!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to B by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=hand-me-some-tissues">hand-me-some-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-arc">netgalley-edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=didn-t-see-that-coming">didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=in-a-name-challenge">in-a-name-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=gimme-the-next-book">gimme-the-next-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288585730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13153624586968003739">*sigh*. This is going to be a hard review to write, but here’s my attempt at writing a review for Masque of the Red Death, even though I know it will not do it justice. <br/><br/>I’ll start off with saying this: <b>I. Loved. This. Book.</b> I loved it with a burning passion, I loved it from the first page, all the way to the last. There was honestly not one moment of this book that I didn’t love. <br/><br/>As I’m writing this review, I’m overcome with so many emotions I’ve received from this book. I cried a little when re</span>
  <span id="freeText13153624586968003739" style="display:none">*sigh*. This is going to be a hard review to write, but here’s my attempt at writing a review for Masque of the Red Death, even though I know it will not do it justice. <br /><br />I’ll start off with saying this: <b>I. Loved. This. Book.</b> I loved it with a burning passion, I loved it from the first page, all the way to the last. There was honestly not one moment of this book that I didn’t love. <br /><br />As I’m writing this review, I’m overcome with so many emotions I’ve received from this book. I cried a little when reading this <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[especially when Elise went to give Araby a good-bye kiss <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I laughed a little when reading this, and most of all I was grinning from ear to ear throughout the whole entire book. <br /><br />I love how, from the beginning of the book, I’ve had my opinions set on each and every character, and I thought my opinions were set in stone, but Griffin somehow managed to switch everything up and make my opinions the exact opposite. (Though I still think April is a bit selfish). <br /><br />I wasn’t prepared for an ending like that, and, while it was a bit abrupt, I still loved it. I did not see any of the plot twists coming (I believe there were three, well, at least there were three for me), and what I absolutely loved is that even when Araby finds out the plot twists, she doesn’t flat out say what they are and gives you some time to think, and then you finally realize what the plot twists are on your own. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[An example of that is when Araby met Malcontent, and she noticed that he had a scar across his neck. It took me a minute or two to realize why that was such a big deal, but then it hit me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I really, really loved the characters in this book, especially Araby. She was sweet, thoughtful and caring, and I absolutely loved that about her. Then there’s also Will, who I really liked, and his two siblings, Elise and Harry, whom I loved. Then there’s April, who’s Araby’s best friend, and sister of another main character, Elliott (who I didn’t like at first but ended up really liking in the end), who I think is pretty selfish (when Araby hurt her shoulder severely, April’s reaction was “Aw, you’re never going to be able to wear a backless dress again.” She wasn’t joking). Despite that, she was a good friend to Araby at times, and genuinely cared for her. But of course, there are also the two antagonists of the book, Prince Prospero and Malcontent. The only complaints I have with these two are their names. <br /><br />Prospero I assume comes from the word “prosper”, which means to be successful, so that was kind of a corny name in my mind for someone trying to take over the world, and a malcontent is someone who rebels against an established system, which also applies to the actions of Malcontent’s character. <br /><br />There’s not really much left I have to say about this, other than that I (of course) loved it, and was extremely happy with the way things ended. <br /><br />I sent Bethany Griffin a message asking if there will be a sequel, but I’ve heard that Masque of the Red Death is supposed to be the first book in a trilogy, so I <u>cannot</u> wait for the next two books (I just hope that isn’t a rumor, and that there actually <i>will</i> be more books to come, but it kind of leaves with an open ending, and everyone planning to do… something that I can’t say, so there has to be another book. Right? Please say right). <br /><br />Highly recommended to <u>absolutely everyone</u>.<br /><br />And if you still aren’t convinced to read this, would it help if I told you that there’s:<br /><br />Crocodiles, bats, masquerade balls, poisonings, treason, some romance, lots of action, icky diseases, and an awesome world? <br /><br />Please tell me that convinced you. <br /><br /><b>UPDATE:</b><br /><br />I just got a response from Bethany Griffin saying that the series will be with two books, and book two will take place less than five minutes after the events of Masque of the Red Death. Book two will be released in April of 2013! (Can't wait!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13153624586968003739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235399695" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235399695" />
    <a title="Rane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1987431-rane"><img alt="Rane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419878997p2/1987431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235399695?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rane" href="/user/show/1987431-rane">Rane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1987431-rane?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235399695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18129050402994502162"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> Based on Poe's dark story of never cheating Death, Bethany Griffin's Masque of the Red Death set in a world where disease has ravage the land and it's people. Streets are filled with death and corpse collectors come to take the dead away. The rich who wear porcelain masks, blank faces that walk the streets and protect the wearer from disease, waste their times at clubs, waiting for death themselves....<br/><br/> Araby is part of this protected rich because of her father the inventor of these masks has gi</span>
  <span id="freeText18129050402994502162" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> Based on Poe's dark story of never cheating Death, Bethany Griffin's Masque of the Red Death set in a world where disease has ravage the land and it's people. Streets are filled with death and corpse collectors come to take the dead away. The rich who wear porcelain masks, blank faces that walk the streets and protect the wearer from disease, waste their times at clubs, waiting for death themselves....<br><br> Araby is part of this protected rich because of her father the inventor of these masks has given her the privilege. Araby though suffers from guilt of just being alive after the death of her twin. As she wastes her days just trying to go numb in the Debauchery Club, she's thrown into the plan of uprising against the sadistic Prince Prospero. <br><br> The world of MOTRD was at times very vague, perhaps a homage to Poe's original story? Nevertheless this gave the story a slow start, the focus was on the damage the disease has done to the world and in the YA genre this is pretty common place. Slowly the world starts to bloom, with danger around every corner, and the small element of steampunk added a great element. Soon the focus lands on the people.<br><br> Araby was an usual character who I grew to like, while at times I wish she just wouldn't get swept away by the tide, she showed alot strengths in her love, loyalty and big heart as she does what she can for those around her. <br> Like many of the characters, a dark cloud of death always looms over any true happiness, but there are bright moments of hope that pull at the reader's heart and gives hope even in the darkness hour.<br><br> The characters prove their not just two dimensional, this of course leads to the two main guys in Araby's life that brings her out of her numbness Elliott and Will. I am not a fan of love triangles, even when the good ones, and this is a good one. Both have their positive and negative and I truly couldn't pick one over the other. Araby often gets caught in their webs, and their actions always left me cold with the pain and heartbreak they caused. This only proved they were just human, and with any relationship trust in earn and broken just as easily. <br> <br> The great lead up toward the end left me frustrated and hungry for more. The almost sudden ending would have been better if it had a slow wind down or an extra chapter. <br> <br> While I greatly enjoyed the book, and look forward to see what Griffin has in store. I just couldn't get over the elements that made me wanna pull my hair out. And perhaps many things will be resolved or made stronger the sequel...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380363145ra/714395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="18129050402994502162" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_225668777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225668777" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3736122-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524600311p2/3736122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225668777?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/3736122-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=harper-collins">harper-collins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3736122-katie?shelf=steampunk-dieselpunk">steampunk-dieselpunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225668777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1624757022286078096">Similar Books: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6234910-the-iron-thorn' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Iron Thorn</a> by Caitlin Kittredge, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10048874-dearly-departed' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dearly, Departed</a> by Lia Habel<br/><br/>Honestly, I'm not really sure how to review this book. It wasn't what I was expecting at all. And while it started off a little bizarre for me and I had a difficult time getting into it, by the end, I was racing through the pages and had to know what happened.<br/><br/>First, let me say that I'm a little confused by this new subgenre of "dystopian steampunk," like <i>Dearly, Departed</i> by Lia Habel. Because the world in Bethany Gr</span>
  <span id="freeText1624757022286078096" style="display:none">Similar Books: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6234910-the-iron-thorn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Iron Thorn</a> by Caitlin Kittredge, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10048874-dearly-departed" rel="nofollow noopener">Dearly, Departed</a> by Lia Habel<br /><br />Honestly, I'm not really sure how to review this book. It wasn't what I was expecting at all. And while it started off a little bizarre for me and I had a difficult time getting into it, by the end, I was racing through the pages and had to know what happened.<br /><br />First, let me say that I'm a little confused by this new subgenre of "dystopian steampunk," like <i>Dearly, Departed</i> by Lia Habel. Because the world in Bethany Griffin's novel has been ravaged by plague, it has that desolate, post-apocalyptic feel of a dystopian. Also, it doesn't have very strong ties to the past such as books like <i>Clockwork Angel</i>, by Cassie Clare. For this reason, I had a difficult time getting a feel for this world that we're thrown into.<br /><br />Also, this book is INCREDIBLY dark. You're probably rolling your eyes right now, thinking, "Well, of course it is! It's based on an Edgar Allan Poe short story!" And that's true, but maybe I wasn't ready for the bleakness of Masque since I'd read <i>Nevermore</i>, by Kelly Creagh, which is fairly upbeat for such dark subject matter.<br /><br />Because this book is DARK! I mean, we're talking, bodies strewn all over the streets. Babies getting thrown onto carts that carry the dead. Drugs. A prince who threatens to feed his nephew to crocodiles. Madness.<br /><br />Take this quote, for example:<br /><br /><i>"I knew a boy who lived with the contagion...Everyone waited for him to die, but he didn't even seem sick, certainly wasn't bedridden. Instead people who came in contact with him died. At first it was deemed coincidence. When his own mother came down with the contagion, he hung himself." (p.172)</i><br /><br />Poe would be proud.<br /><br />But in the midst of this bizarre world, you've got Araby. It takes us quite a while for us to really get to know her. I had a difficult time sympathizing with her at first, because she's so bent on numbing herself to all emotions. She takes drugs so she doesn't have to deal with the guilt of her brother's death or interact with her parents, who are just as jacked up as she is.<br /><br />Even at the end of the book, I didn't feel that connected to Araby. Although she had a clear character motivation and I could understand why she did what she did, there was just no spark of life in her that propelled me to care about her.<br /><br />Most of the other characters were flat, as well. You've got Will, the mysterious boy who works at the Debauchery Club but who also takes care of his little brother and sister because their parents are dead. And then there's Elliott, the brother of Araby's best friend who also happens to be the nephew of Prince Prospero. We're never really sure if Elliott is crazy or not. Sometimes, he seems it, sometimes not. Honestly, though I got the feeling we were supposed to be disturbed by Elliott, I felt the most connection to him. He seemed the most real out of everyone.<br /><br />But what this book lacks in character development, it makes up for in beauty of language and overall plot. Griffin's real strength is in her ability to craft language. I was often given flashbacks to reading <i>Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone</i>, by Laini Taylor (and that's high praise!). The simple, subdued way Griffin expressed Araby's emotions was beautiful, and I was often struck by a particularly poignant passage that was about nothing more than eating breakfast or walking down the street.<br /><br />I also thought the plotting and pacing were really well done. The book slowly builds to a powerful climax that left me at the end of the story wanting more. The last chapter in particular was really great, and it made me want book 2 like, yesterday.<br /><br />Overall, this is a more literary book than I was expecting. It's got a great voice that haunted me even after I'd finished it. Although the characters were a little lacking, I was intrigued enough by the worldbuilding and the beautiful prose to enjoy it, and I look forward to book 2!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1624757022286078096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/264202391" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/264202391?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264202391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15269396319157622535"><b>Rating:</b> 3.5 creepy-yet-gorgeous stars out of 5!<br/><br/>Dark. Dangerous. Lyrical. Tragic. Poe would be so proud of this book! <br/><br/>Set in a plagued city with danger around every corner, <b>Masque of the Red Death</b> is one of the most chilling yet captivating dystopians I've ever read. There's death wherever you turn; corpse collectors roam the dangerous streets. And everyone has to wear a porcelain mask outside to protect them from the plague, but only the rich can afford them. <br/><br/>Araby is such a heartbroken and hear</span>
  <span id="freeText15269396319157622535" style="display:none"><b>Rating:</b> 3.5 creepy-yet-gorgeous stars out of 5!<br /><br />Dark. Dangerous. Lyrical. Tragic. Poe would be so proud of this book! <br /><br />Set in a plagued city with danger around every corner, <b>Masque of the Red Death</b> is one of the most chilling yet captivating dystopians I've ever read. There's death wherever you turn; corpse collectors roam the dangerous streets. And everyone has to wear a porcelain mask outside to protect them from the plague, but only the rich can afford them. <br /><br />Araby is such a heartbroken and heart<i>break</i>ing character. With the guilt of her twin brother's death hanging over her, she refuses to let herself to be happy, to experience anything he won't. While my heart goes out to Araby for what she goes through, this makes is a little harder to connect with her. I had the same problem with most of the other characters. We only skimmed the surface when I felt like there was so much more beneath their masks. <br /><br />The romance was twisted yet incredibly sweet — just like the two boys. There are secrets, sacrifices, and huge surprises you won't expect. Bethany Griffin <i>knows</i> how to write suspense! And even though I wish there was more of a punch to that build-up, it still left me craving to know how anything could possibly work out in this bleak world. <br /><br />Deliciously dark and hauntingly beautiful, <b>Masque of the Red Death</b> sits up there with Kelly Creagh's <b>Nevermore</b> on my list of coolest Poe-inspired books! It wasn't as mind-blowing as I'd hoped, but it still stuck with me and I can't wait to read the next. :)<br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> Edgar Allan Poe fans, get ready to empty your wallets! Don't let the rating fool you — this book is definitely worth the read! Am I the only one hoping this will be turned into a movie? x) <br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/04/review-masque-of-red-death.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>

<div id="review_589271765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer3895421057343170616">A decent Edgar Allan Poe inspired YA steampunk dystopian romance. The world building is pretty great although slow as we get to know Araby's depressingly atmospheric city. Araby herself is quite flawed and on paper she should be a fascinating lead, but she's quite underwhelming and I wasn't all that interested in her the further I got through the story. Now, just to warn you, there is a love triangle which got old - Araby is very indecisive. I didn't really care about Will one way or another in </span>
  <span id="freeText3895421057343170616" style="display:none">A decent Edgar Allan Poe inspired YA steampunk dystopian romance. The world building is pretty great although slow as we get to know Araby's depressingly atmospheric city. Araby herself is quite flawed and on paper she should be a fascinating lead, but she's quite underwhelming and I wasn't all that interested in her the further I got through the story. Now, just to warn you, there is a love triangle which got old - Araby is very indecisive. I didn't really care about Will one way or another in the long run, but Elliott makes the story. He's definitely more of an intriguing character than even our MC. Overall, I doubt I'll be back for the sequel. However, I do highly recommend Bethany Griffin's <i>The Fall</i> which retell Poe's classic short story "The Fall of the House of Usher" from Madeleine's point of view.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539827623ra/26464674.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_253857546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253857546" />
    <a title="Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke"><img alt="Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476044114p2/4140635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253857546?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253857546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2757705419292983686">Oh my GOODNESS!! How can it end like that?!! AHH! Really, really good book! I NEED more! :)<br/><br/>I was not expecting to fall for Masque of the Red Death as hard as I did! I loved every page, every character and ever plot twist. This book was simply fantastic!<br/><br/>The world in which this story takes place is a dark one. Where death is a daily occurrence and rain is almost always on the downpour the whole book has this very eerie vibe to it. The setting and mood really played its own role throughout the whol</span>
  <span id="freeText2757705419292983686" style="display:none">Oh my GOODNESS!! How can it end like that?!! AHH! Really, really good book! I NEED more! :)<br /><br />I was not expecting to fall for Masque of the Red Death as hard as I did! I loved every page, every character and ever plot twist. This book was simply fantastic!<br /><br />The world in which this story takes place is a dark one. Where death is a daily occurrence and rain is almost always on the downpour the whole book has this very eerie vibe to it. The setting and mood really played its own role throughout the whole story and i loved that!<br /><br />I also really liked the main character Araby! She's a super compassionate character and she puts all of her emotions into every decision she makes (even when she tries not to.) She cares so deeply about everyone she knows and she’s not above giving out second chances. But she’s also extremely guarded and closed off. She puts up this front and tends to hide who she really is from others. So to escape not only the terrors of the outside world but also her inner struggles, Araby goes to local debauchery club on a regular basis with her friend April.<br /><br />There, Araby meets Will and Oh. My. Perfection. He is everything you could ever possibly want in a fictional boy. Holy Gods. Jus...UNFF! (And that’s a technical term...) He has this unruly dark hair, a sly smile AND he’s all tatted up. *THUD* All of those glorious attributes make him totally mysterious, seriously sexy, and slightly dangerous.<br /><br />Which makes it even more surprising when Will takes Araby back to his home. When she gets there, she learns that Will’s parents died from the plague leaving him to take care of his little brother, Henry, and little sister, Elise. And that was absolutely endearing to read about. He is so good to them and so protective that it made me want to cry. I could feel how much they meant to him through the pages. GAH! I just want to marry this boy. He’s completely charming and sweet and he’s someone that Araby really opens up to and starts to not only trust, but fall for as well. But, Will is not without faults...and I’ll leave that tidbit right there...<br /><br />When Will’s not around another boy seems to always be close by...April’s brother, Elliot. *sighs* Oh, Elliot, you semi-insane stud with a hero complex, how could I not also grow attached to you too? This boy has issues—major issues. Issues so deep that it seems almost impossible to get through to him. He’s arrogant and stubborn and selfish, but something about him drew me in. And it also drew Araby in as well.<br /><br />When it comes to the boys in this book, picking a team is out of the question. The love triangle is done so amazingly well that I have no words as to describe its brilliance.<br /><br />With an intense ending and no clear-cut future for Araby, I’m dying for more of her story! Masque of the Red Death is a stunning, seductive and incredible novel! I HIGHLY recommend it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2757705419292983686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4786727473693364905" style="display:none">I have been waiting for a book like this for forever! I don’t even know where to begin I just loved this! It was creepy, gothic (thanks Giselle =P), dark, icky, depressing, and just all out amazing. <br /><br />Set in a time where a plaque like disease has almost wiped out the humans Abray lives the life that most don’t. She has a porcelain mask that helps protect her from the germs that cause this disease. When her best friend is taken she is asked to help find her and help in a rebellion against the evil Prince. With no other alternatives she gives her trust to Elliot and so starts her journey to uncovering many many truths that she never saw coming.<br /><br />I have to say this book was right up my alley. I love a good story that has twists and boy oh boy this one delivers. At one point my mouth actually dropped because I never saw that punch coming! It was brilliant. I am really at a loss for words with this one because it was just that good. My review will never do the book justice. Please pick this book up you won’t regret it at all! I give the author major credit for writing such a depressing book but making it so intricate and detailed that the reader just wants to hope for the best in every situation.<br /></span>

<div id="review_646178911" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646178911" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646178911?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst">watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-concept-poor-execution">great-concept-poor-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646178911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8488577960684936710"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824938._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824939._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>No, not really. I never had braces.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824940.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yes, I know. You all have the right to hate me now.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393644348ra/8745433.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What I had when I was thirteen was far worse than braces; <b>I had a huge stick up my ass.</b> Yes, I admit it and I can laugh at myself now, but the me back then was insufferable. If I could go back in time, I'd give myself a sound slap across the face to see if I could knock that stick out. <br/><br/>I walked around thinking I was better than everyone (I wasn't), and everyone else were provincial losers (they weren't</span>
  <span id="freeText8488577960684936710" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824938._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824939._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, not really. I never had braces.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824940.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, I know. You all have the right to hate me now.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393644348ra/8745433.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I had when I was thirteen was far worse than braces; <b>I had a huge stick up my ass.</b> Yes, I admit it and I can laugh at myself now, but the me back then was insufferable. If I could go back in time, I'd give myself a sound slap across the face to see if I could knock that stick out. <br><br>I walked around thinking I was better than everyone (I wasn't), and everyone else were provincial losers (they weren't). As an indirect result, I became the kind of girl that people call emo. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824941._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I could give Sasuke a run for his money.<br><br>I wore black all the time, I didn't like going out <s>in the sunlight</s>, and I <i>loathed</i> having my picture taken. You can imagine how my birthday party went down.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401629492ra/9824942.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thankfully, somewhere along the line, I grew the fuck up and learned that the world is not all about MEMEMEMEMEMEMEMEME! I ditched black for red dresses and pastel-colored tank tops. I still prefer staying at home over bars, but I'd accompany my friends out. I also take the occasional selfie now. Yay!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401629492i/9824943._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only thing that remained of that 13-year-old angsty girl was her love of horror, which I still indulge in regularly, though less than before. <b>I was a huge Edger Allen Poe fan (still am, actually), so Masque of the Red Death, a reimagining of Poe's classic tale of the same name, caught my attention immediately.</b> I expected a gothic story ridden with plague, and perhaps a Phantom of the Opera element as the Red Death.<br><br><b>This book delivered...but I didn't like it.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401417443ra/9800198.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>A large part of the reason is the narrator, Araby. Being in her head was like reliving my tween years.</b> She's dreary. She shuns new experiences because of a tragic accident involving her deceased brother, and seeks oblivion through drugs. She just doesn't want to do<i> anything</i> with her life; a living corpse.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381219773ra/4553350.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I understand this is part of her character and she displays a tremendous amount of character development later on. Her devotion to her dead brother is misguided but sympathetic. But I still can't get past the icky feeling that I'm supposed to root for, and love, a character I want to punch in the face, a.k.a thirteen-year-old Natalie. This is a supremely personal thing, but one that affects my whole perception of the book.<br><br><b>The love interests, Will and Elliot, failed to win my affection and seemed rather bland as characters.</b> Honestly, I can't tell the two apart at all. There's a love triangle too, though to be fair, it didn't really get on my nerves. Araby and the boys care more about saving their city than their tangled loves lives, and Araby doesn't whine on about who to choose, which is good.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401629492ra/9824944.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only character I like is April, Araby's best friend. <br><b>At first, I thought she was going to be another ditzy-best-friend-type because she likes make-up, dresses and parties, but it turns out there is a surprisingly large amount of depth to her.<br></b> When she first met Araby, she saved her from jumping off the edge of a building, and remains calm and reliable during the siege even though <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she was infected with the plague. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She's a well-rounded out and interesting character on her own, and I sort of wish the story had been told from her POV than Araby's.<br><br><b>Also, I didn't like the overall style of the book.</b> I like my literature with punch and sizzle, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17345314.Cracked__Soul_Eater___1_" title="Cracked (Soul Eater, #1) by Eliza Crewe" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked</a> rather than the dreamy quality of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12930909.Between_the_Devil_and_the_Deep_Blue_Sea__Between___1_" title="Between the Devil and the Deep Blue Sea (Between, #1) by April Genevieve Tucholke" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the Devil and the Deep Blue Sea</a>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391549133ra/8409135.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, not a bad book, but failed to spark my interest. If you're a fan of gothic novels and Poe, you might enjoy this. Otherwise, stand clear.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8488577960684936710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4505299188549244413" style="display:none">Star Rating system:<br />5 stars: LOVE LOVE LOVE The book is perfect in my perspective<br />4 stars: LIKE LOVE LIKE The book is amazing but has it's flaws<br />3 stars: OKAY LIKE OKAY The book is interesting enough to read but did not love it<br />2 stars: NAH OKAY NAH The book is boring but manage to read it<br />1 stars: NAH NAH NAH The book is poor did not like it a bit<br /><br />This book is started off really slow it took me like 4 days to read it (on average i finish 2 days even with school)<br />The plot was extremely boring 60% in and nothing really seems to happen, it was only towards the ending I'm drawn to the book. <br /><br />Is this book suppose to be dark and twisted? I think so. But NO. <br /><br />As much as I'm not a gothic or horror story reader and considering the fact that I get scared easily. This book literally feels like reading a love story more that anything *sighs* From a certain point I started treating this book as a romance novel xD <br /><br />Luckily I did not hate any characters but I did not like them them enough to care for them. However I do have to say the relationships between the characters feels real enough, meanwhile the love triangle wasn't the best it has served its purpose. <br /><br />Though I did not love this book, I'm kinda interested to know what happen next. So I was actually planning to read the second one, BUT the reviews were not to pleasing. <br /><br />Overall I'm satisfy with the book, it was an interesting read. I would recommend it to anyone who likes "dark" romance, but if you are finding a scary intense read this is not the book for you. <br /><br />P.s The dark romance is not really dark, but since it is a gothic novel it call it dark <br /><br />Hopes this helps :DD</span>
